Oh, my children, now that I have completed this book, which is the last of medical science, through its completion you may find its end within it, and by its explanations and declarations, it is evident to me that I have composed this treatise for you, which is part of my surgical operations.
Since the surgical operation of the hand is practiced in our region and in our time almost entirely privately, despite the importance of its science and the difficulty of acquiring it; and there have been only occasional brief descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which have corrected many errors and hesitations but have closed off understanding of it and lengthened its study and art.
And it is clear to me that I should enliven that order in this treatise according to the way of explanation and declaration and abbreviation; and for the forms of the cautery tools and other instruments of the work to be added through the declaration and preparation, which cause is necessary.
More so, the reason why a good craftsman does not use his hand well in this our time is that the art of medicine is long and drawn out, and one must be trained beforehand to understand anatomy, which Galen knew well, recognizing the youthfulness of the members and their forms, as well as their joints and separations; and he had knowledge of the bones, nerves, and sinews, their number and their diseases; and of the pulsating veins and quiet ones, and the places of their effusion.
And for this, Hippocrates is said to be silent in the short work, but more so in the art of the hand.
More so, we have already spoken of this in the introduction to this book; for those who do not know what we said about anatomy, will surely fall into error because of it, and many people have died as a result, as I have seen too many such cases. For some are formed in this science but throw themselves into that other science and its experiments.
For I have seen a foolish and inexperienced doctor who, by mistake, caused an apostematosis scrophulosa in the neck of a woman, and damaged some arteries so that great blood loss occurred; the woman died among her many sufferings.
And there is another doctor who nearly removed a stone from a man who had suffered in his condition, and the stone was large, and it came to him, and he dried that stone with a piece of the bladder.
And I have already called for it to be extracted, and I saw that due to the size of the stone and the position of the patient, he would die.
And there was another doctor who took a stipend from a duke of our land for surgery, and arrived at a blacksmith named Negro who had suffered a fracture in his thigh; and because of the doctor's ignorance, he extracted the fracture, over the wound, with pillows and stakes of strong structure, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
And then let it slip according to his desires, and then reattach, and then leave it alone for a few days as commanded that we release the bandage; and thus remain until the thigh and foot recover, and proceed to heal.
And I was called to him, and prepared to untie the ligament, and tranquility and an attempt to relieve his pains was achieved.
But still, since corruption was confirmed in the member, I could not contain that, and did not cease to walk the corruption through the member while the illness persisted.
And I saw another doctor who incised a cancerous abscess, and it became ulcerated for several days, during which the malignancy of the lesion increased in the lord.
The cause is that the pain is purely due to melancholic humors, and does not affect the entire body, but rather affects a member that suffers from being attacked by all.
And for this reason, my son, it is necessary for you that the operation be devised in two ways: one where the operation is associated with health, and another where the work is perilous in its major considerations.
And I have already existed in this entire treatise where the operation is associated with error and fear; therefore, it is necessary for you to keep this and leave that, so that the leaves do not find a way to speak ill of you.
And therefore take your arms with diligence and protection of God, and your patients with happiness and firmness.
And use the best way by the grace of God seeking salvation and the praiseworthy success, and lay aside the terrible illnesses difficult to cure, and place your arms in that which fears you, so that sitting in your faith and in your name you do not fail: for more remains to your glory, and less elsewhere in the world and beyond in your sanctity.
Gualia already dissected in some monastic sources: Do not treat evil illness, lest bad doctors be named.
And I have already devoted this libel according to three chapters.
Begin the division of the book, and first of the first part. The first chapter ordered of the foot, in the forms of the instruments and in the tools of the cautery, and of what is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, on drying and perforation, and on cups, and on plaigs, and on extraction of arrows and similar, all categorized and ordered by the forms of the instruments.
The third chapter, on restoration and dislocation, and on the cure of tortoises and similar; a chapter ordered by the head between the feet, and by the forms of the instruments.
First, I will describe the quality of the coals for the cautery and their effects, and in which condition cautery is prohibited.
Therefore, I say that the discourse on the quality of the cautery coal and its effects is long and tedious, subtle through science, and a hidden secret; many wise men have spoken much about it, and they are in disagreement. For me, a little from their sermons suffices, as I fear the length.
And therefore it is said that a cautery is applied to the entire complexity universally which is of flesh or sinew, except for two complexities, which are complexities of sinew.
In the complexity of sinew and dry flesh, they will desiccate; for some said that a cautery is beneficial for this, while others said the opposite, that a cautery is not suitable in illness which is due to quality and dryness, for the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and it is inconvenient that an illness of sinew and dry flesh be healed by what is cautery and dry.
And say that those who say the opposite, that by cautery healing is done in all sinew and dry illness that comes in men's bodies, for when you compare the body of man to the elements of his body to the complexity of fire, you find the body is dry.
And I say according to his speech, for I have experienced this myself several times to confirm it.
But I do not consider that it comes to me who is already experienced in the practice of cautery through recent exercise, and who has known the diversity of human complexity and the disposition of illnesses in their manifestations, and the causes of those, and the accidents related to them, and the duration of those.
In other complications, it is not about your fear, and especially in wet and cold diseases, for all doctors are agreed on those, and they do not differ in applying cautery to them in youth.
Know, sons, that concerning the secret of curing by cautery with fire and its goodness, on the burning cautery medicine, it is because the fire is simple, its action reaching only the member being cauterized and not affecting other members only to a small harm.
But the action of the burning medicine reaches that part in the members where it touches, and strongly causes illness in the member that is difficult to heal and rapidly exacerbates it.
But fire, by its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not cause anything other than to superfluously burn. We have known this through experience and long service studying the art on the true causes; and for this reason, I am excused for the length of my discourse. If it were not that this is not written at my leisure in this pause, and if I did not reveal to you your secret about fire, its quality in operations and the way it expels diseases, I would use a philosophical demonstration, which would be acute in your ears.
And be wise, sons, that they do not disagree about the time when it is convenient to make a cautery and pause the best season of spring.
And I say that a cautery is convenient at all times, because the damage from the accidental season is submerged in the youth of what is burned by the cautery, and especially if the cautery is for pains or necessary pains, strong sores, which do not suffer delay because it is feared that those caused by malice are greater than small damage entering through time.
And this is not done on your parts, or, sons, those who do not esteem it but the common people and the foolish doctors, since for that illness which is cured by cautery it is not always ready, and they pause that consequence.
And the cause is not thus because they care for this, for a cautery is not other than in place of medicine which alters the composition and dries the humors which are the cause that wind brings pain.
Yet, however, excessive cautery over medicine for the expediency of its efficacy and virtue of its operation and greatness of its lord.
And it is possible that the patient's illness returns at some point in time, according to the complexity of the illness and the location of the illness, and its virtue, and what is prepared in the body from the aggregation of superfluities within it, and what is acquired in the body through food and semblance of those causes; but the illness where a cautery is administered is a subtle illness in a member with few superfluities and humidities, just as a dental cautery for pain and similar to that, it is possible that that pain does not return in it, but this is done in small amounts.
And more common speech is that the cautery is the last remedy of medicine, and it is a term used by those who do not understand it, for I believe it is not a cure that helps either from medicine or any other cause except the cautery.
And the cause is contrary to this; and the understanding that the cautery is the last remedy of medicine is only when one administers the methods of cure in some illnesses, and those medicines are not effective, and at the end of the illness, one administers the cautery, which helps then. And at this point from here, the last remedy of medicine is a cautery, not according to the understanding which I understand the vulgar and most of the foolish doctors.
And the ancients said that a cautery of gold is better than one made of iron, and they did not say this only because of the equality of gold and its sublime nature.
And they said that the place for cautery does not burn, since it is not absolutely charred; for I have already examined this and have observed that it does not do so in all bodies as in others, and a gold cautery is good and better than iron as they say; yet when you make a cautery with fire of gold, it has not been declared to you, for it ignites according to the quantity you want due to the reactivity of gold, and prepares to receive flame; if you adjust over the ignition, the gold melts by the fire, and it settles in the fire on some sheets so that the craftsman can cut through its occupation.
And for this, you should make the cautery of iron lighter and more precisely to the right position during the operation.
And I have already ordered this chapter concerning the cautery according to chapters, and I have ordered those of the leg within the foot, so that I delay the requester what he wants from me.
The first chapter.
This cautery addresses the cold and humidity over the servel accident of which there are two causes, these being the cause of soda and much trauma from a traumatic flow, called corissa, in the head, to the branches of the neck and to the ears leaking, and much sleepiness, and toothache, and the jaw, and universally all illness that comes from cold, such as paralytically, soda and apoplexy, and semblanz in those illnesses.
The form of this cautery is as follows: Primarily, you command the patient to be evacuated with a purgative medicine for three or four nights, according to the virtue needed by the patient, the age of the patient, and the patient's habits.
And then command those who shave his head to do so with scissors, and place that sezer between your hands on a lowered bench and have their hands rest on their own foot.
And then place the edge of your palm razor near his foot between his toes. More over, since the true location is found, mark that location with a pinch, and then heat the olive cautery of which this is the form:
And then place that cautery over the marked location with a pinch, in such a way that it descends gradually, and your hand is gradually constrained, while you rotate it.
And then lift your hand slightly and look at the location. If you see any part of the bone being revealed, as much as the amount of error, then lift your hand. If not, return your hand to that iron or another, if it is cooled, so that what I have said about it can be seen from the bone.
And then take a little of salt and dissolve it over the area and leave it for three days.
And then place your hand over the inguinal wound and leave it there until the scar of the fire is destroyed. And then treat the area with an ointment of tetrafarmakon until it is healed.
And we have said that when the wound is opened wide, it heals better, for it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them say that the condyle should be cauterized inside the bone, and that the cautery should remain until it has fused with a part of the bone.
And then scrape what is attached to the bone, and then treat it.
And others say that the cautery should reach the marrow, pressing strongly on the bone until the bone cools, and this is the method of Alphécatii petit. And they estimate from that place exhale the vapors of the head.
And let the wound be kept open for a long time, and then cure it once it is consolidated.
But I have not seen these two types of cautery for all cases, only in some men out of fear; and leave that one, I advise you, it is better to be salted when it is, because the head is heated by solution of continuity of the sun as we have testified in other members, especially when the head of the patient is of cold nature.
And the first type of cautery is safer and better, I advise you; use that one and perform that operation with salt.
Capitulate second.
On the cautery for the head.
When throughout the head there occurs chronic and long-lasting pain that has been prolonged in the patient, and they use cloths, beans, head poultices, plaisters, ointments, hens' combs, cotton, and linens, and especially if the head has already been cauterized with a cautery which does not improve from any of these causes, then consider whether the head of the patient is of strong constitution in its nature; and there is no great cold or heat, then that cautery should be replaced by another. And then cauterize that on the top of his head between where the vein is divided. Incise the vein and expose the quantity which we have counted, and cauterize that with a cautery at the back of the head in the place where it is called vas, — and this is the place where suction is applied. And lift your hand here, and do not expose the bone, for the gout by this finds great pain different from the pain of all other cautery marks on the head.
And I will say this cautery in its place, for I know that the cautery on which one cauterizes the horns of the head and the occiput is a finer cautery than that on which the middle part of the head is cauterized; and this is the form of it.
Capitulum terminatum.
On the cautery treatment for new migraines.
When there is a sharp pain in the back of the head, or a stabbing pain inside the ear, the head should be treated with medicines that purify the brain, and the other treatment, which I have described for diseases, should be administered; and if this does not help, then cauterization can be performed in two ways: either with a sharp burning medicine, or with iron.
May a cautery that burns in medicine be that you take a hot coal, hold it there, and abrade the extremities of it from both ends. Then apply the place of the pain in the temple with a lancet laid between it, make the cut there, and let the needle be concealed.
Then strengthen over the place stopped by descent compression, and leave it for the space of three hours; then remove the bandage, and leave the wound for two or three days, and then place over the cut submerge in a border until the place dries up.
Then cure that with ointment while it is healing.
And if you wish, do what some burning medicines allow, which I have written in the second treatise of burning medicines.
May the cautery be done according to this manner: heat by cautery of which this is the form:
and it is called clavicle, for its head has the form of a small blade and in the middle location there is a slight prominence.
Then place your hand over the location of the pain, and hold it back—so that the artery which is left is not burned—and slowly rotate the small iron tool.
And if the quantity that is burned due to the depth of the wound is significant, lift your hand so that the artery which is left is not burned, to prevent bleeding.
Then soak it in salt water and place it over the area, leaving it for three days. Then place it like a warm bandage, and keep it treated with ointment until it heals.
And if you do, cauterize at the end of the surgical blade according to the cautery, and be careful to avoid cutting the artery in this new migrainous condition.

Place the line where you feel the pain along its length, or approximately there; then hold your hand firmly for a moment and incise the artery and pierce through to the bone.
However, you must be careful of the continuity of the jaw, which is weakened by mastication, and ensure that the ligament is not adhered and the nerves which supply it are intact, and that no spasm occurs.
And if it concerns the care and precaution of the flow of blood from the artery that is severed, for in its severing there is fear, especially for one who ignores what he does and is not studious or careful; and leaves the operation at the beginning.
And I will bring to memory the regulation of the flow of blood in relation to the artery according to its manner, in this place of this livre.
And if you see this illness in someone who cannot bear this cautery and you see the condition of the patient tolerable, apply the cautery in the middle of the foot as we have recounted, and treat the wound until it is healed.

Chapter V.
On the cautery for headaches.
When there is pain in the ear due to cold and it is treated with conservative causes and another treatment as mentioned in the division, and the pain does not subside, then apply the cautery, which is called the puncta. This is its form:
And then puncture near the beginning, and be led to the outer ear as if a wheel is rotated, or in the circuit of each place if the pain is in any part. Lengthen the cautery from the root of the ear gradually until you have found the location and tested it.
And if the cautery touches all points in the ear, and you stop there, then thoroughly cure the areas between until they are healed.
Chapter VI.
On the cautery for the ear.
The ear condition, which is cured and treated with a cautery, is only due to substances carried by phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases.
Avoid using a cautery for the substance that causes dryness or spasms of the nerve.
When you cure that type of ear condition with jerris, capipurgi, and guaragismes, and your treatment does not show results, then you must use three cauteries: the first on the root of the ear, the second a small mark on its temple, and the third on the junction of two lips.
And place your cautery on the opposite side of the affected area, for relief only occurs in the part that is healthy.
The method of cautery is to apply the cautery to the outer part of the ear near the tip, placing a small piece over the corner of the head, and on the temple, the length of which should be according to the length of the hand's breadth, and then place your hand over the cautery until the quantity of the substance of the conifer has been burned.
This is the method of the cautery, and it is specific to the barber-surgeon, whose form is described below. But more subtly, you should see just a little bit less than what you can perceive; and cut away just a little to avoid excess.
And then treat the area with what is described until it is healed.

The method of cauterization is performed as described above.

Chapter XVI.
Of the cautery for the eyelid when the skin is converted to the inner parts and palm of the hand.
When the skin of the eyelid is converted to the inner parts, I must puncture the eyelid. The cautery for this can be performed in two ways: either by a hot cautery or by applying a burning medicine.
If using a hot cautery, command the patient to look away from where the skin is to be burned as one would when cleansing the skin, ensuring it is thoroughly and evenly applied; and if puncturing, place the point at the origin of the eyelid. Then strengthen the eyelids with a bandage so that they do not tear before the skin has healed.
Then, once the skin is healed and even, place the head of the patient on a pillow, and then apply heat to the eyelids, marking the area with a mark shaped like a laurel leaf, which will be the starting point of the incision for the skin.
And then place something hot in the abdomen or on the bladder over the belly.
And then heat the cautery, of which this is the form.
And then cauterize over the figure which is marked, little by little in small squares, while the surface of the wound, which is like a laurel leaf, is completely burned.
And a sign of health from your work is that you see the eyelid of the belly already contracted and the skin around it raised from the puncture of the belly.
And then lift your hand and leave it for three days, and then place it again carefully on the spot between where the scar is healing. And then apply ointment until it heals.
But if it returns through the skin for some cause near their origin and the eyelid becomes softened, then apply the cautery again to that area just as you did at first.
If the skin is on the eyelid, then cauterize it while elevating it to its natural place and ensure that the skin does not blister.
But the cautery with medicine burning it is what you command the patient to stretch the skin while it is elongated and ensured to be even, and then make a leaf-shaped form of paper from cloth.
And then take known soap and fresh fat, or what is instead thereof, and mix these fats well, and prepare this mixture to ensure it is not rubbed; then spread this over the paper which is made thus in the shape of a leaf of mint, and place that over one or both wounds; and place the remaining portion wrapped in cloth, and the patient's head be at the top.
And place the said portion over the medicine and press it slightly so that the patient feels the bite of the medicine, for the bite is like that of fire.
And thus, when the patient perceives that the bite of the medicine, then leave the medicine and place it at the top as just said; therefore, when the bite ceases, then put back the medicine and wash the wound with water; and then consider if the eyelid has already been raised, if so, you should constrict it with fire or incision, for then this is good; and if not, return to the application of the medicine at the place where it did not press and ensure that your operation remains even and contracts the wound.
And then place your hand over the side where the adhesion's bond is to be removed, and cure that with an ointment or something else in which it may be healed.
And you must, in your operation, keep careful vigilance that no mistake of medicine fall into it. If the eyelid becomes softened and some cause of the skin pustules on the eyelid, then repeatedly apply your medicine to that place which has become softened, and do so precisely as you did at the beginning, and soon let it heal.
This is the way to prepare the willow leaf.
And know that the eyelids of humans are diverse in size and smallness, and therefore according to this you should make your incision.
And the way to straighten it should not be hidden from those who study in this art.
Capitol. xvii.
On the cautery treatment of a fistula in the lacrimal gland of the eyelid.
When you cure a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases and do not bring your cure to completion, then when you cauterize it in this manner: command the patient to place his head on your lap, and have some minister between your laps in such a way that his head is neither hurt nor agitated.
Then place the hot iron on the skin of the calf or over the lump of the ankle on his heel.
Then heat the cautery with which this is done:
which is hollow, such as the shape of a cane or a bird's feather quill, from one end of which the cautery is made.
And if you wish, penetrate into the other end. And if you wish, let it be drawn out like a needle.
However, that which is hollow is better for your work.
And then press the fistula if it is opened, and draw from it clean and dry that which comes out. And if it is not opened, then open it and extract the pus from it.
And then place the well-ignited cautery over it, and hold your hand a little above the nose, so that your hand does not err or the patient is quieted, and then place the cautery on the nostrils and destroy that.
And so, if at the beginning of your cautery it enters into the mouth, that is good; and if not, then iterate the cautery one or two times, as needed; and leave it thus for three days, and then place your hand over that spot to keep it warm and surround it with an ointment until it heals.
And if it has passed ten days and it is not healed, then place your hand over the sharp corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed and removed as you see fit in your treatise.
And another method of cautery for a fistula which some first doctors will say: place it at the location of the fistula and do that and then place your hand on that fissure like a thin form of it. Pour in there the quantity of one ounce of melted lead; hold your hand in good retention, so that the bad humor does not enter through that which the melted lead does not penetrate to that place; cover over the location of the fistula until it is covered as if in white of an egg or in water, for lead adheres to the location of the fistula and heals that through marvelous healing.

Capitol.xxv.
From the roots to the tips of the nose.
Pustules appear at the roots of the nose, and are enlarged and mounded over several days as the pimple becomes visible upon examination.
And for this reason, you should examine it when the pustule first appears, and keep track of it. And then place a covering over the area, or use a cautery or burning medicine where it was located.
But if the examination is delayed until after the pustule has enlarged, consider whether it is hardened, dark in color, and of little sensation. In that case, do not touch it with a sharp object as it may be an abscess; for pustules that you examine at this stage should beware of the great harm they can cause to the person upon whom they have formed.
And if the abscess is due to a blow and not dark in color, and examination is possible throughout the area, then drain the infection and examine it without fear, and treat the area with what dries and constricts until it heals.
Chapter XXVI.
For the suturing of the nose and lips when the continuity is dissolved by plague or similar diseases.
Know that when there is a dissolution of continuity in one of these cartilages, you should not much concern yourself with that operation but rather with some skilled individuals.
Therefore, when you find any cause of these conditions, consider whether it is fresh plague with its own symptoms, and then adjust the two lips of the plague with sutures, and proceed to cure that which remains until it is healed.
And if the lips of dissolution of continuity are already separated, and any one is made healthy, then you should scrape each part of its visible edge until it bleeds with pus. Then adjust the two lips with sutures and strengthen them, and sprinkle dragon's blood powder and thistle over them, and place a piece of transparent plaster or some other consolidative plaster on top of the powder, and leave this mixture for two to three days. Then remove that and change the plaster, leaving it until the roots have resolved themselves, and proceed to apply ointment until it is healed.
The manner of suturing is that you add the solution of continuity or use needles as we have recommended in the belly suture, or add the solution of continuity with thread as you are made to know.
Chapter XXVII.
Of the extraction of those causes that wind enters in the two lips in the parts within.
Slight rashes often appear in the inner parts of the lips and become hard swellings resembling lumps of fat; some are small, while others are larger.
Then carefully remove all parts of the lips and each of those hard swellings, and during the excision fill the area with three threads to tighten the wound, and afterward wash it with wine and treat the area with water that is astringent until it heals.
Chapter XXVIII.
Of the incision of the flesh adhered to the gums.
Great care must be taken over the gums that are tightly attached, which the ancients called albulus, then withdraw that probe or whatever instrument you have used, cleanse that place thoroughly, and let the healthy fluid flow or let it coagulate.
Then place something warm on the area, or other styptic or excitatory powders.
And if that flesh returns, then incise it again, and cauterize it; for afterwards the cauterization will not return.
Capitol.xxix.
On the reason for teeth being firm.
When on the surface of the teeth in both internal and external parts, and between the gums, there are sharp, hard edges, some times they are blackish and are caused by yellow or green substances that corrupt the gums, causing the teeth to become loose.
And therefore, make sure you cut the patient's thigh between your thighs and place the patient's head in a pillow, and rub the teeth where these edges and similar causes appear with some substance that does not cause any harm, and this is done for the blackness and the yellowish coloration and other changes they may have undergone.
Then if what is in those at the beginning of the reasoning is good; and if not, then you iterate the reasoning on those the next day and the second and the third until it comes to the final statement in what you want.
And know that the teeth have required grooves carved in various forms and with diverse figures according to what is prepared for your operation. And so, some razors for which the tooth is shaved from the inside out are different from the razors for which it is shaved between the teeth according to other forms, and these forms of razors you must prepare, which you will often see:
Capitol.xxx.
For the extraction of teeth.
Cure the tooth with all skill and take your time in its extraction, for no cause can compensate for the removal itself when it occurs, as a substance is sublimated during the process of extracting it.
More carefully cure when the gout forces you to extract that tooth, for firmly you must be certain which is the painful tooth, for many removals of pain deceive the gout and mistakenly target a healthy tooth, and you extract that one and soon the pain does not cease until the diseased and painful tooth is extracted, for we have already seen this in the operations of barbers.
Therefore you must be certified which is the painful tooth, and knowing well, when you incise along the circuit of the tooth with spatum in which some virtue may be dissolved from the root of the tooth of all parts, and then near those ties said, or with fine scissors at the beginning gradually until those concussions.
And then apply water to it strongly holding great force for good speech or strong fracture, and place the head of the patient between those ties well that you do not suffocate, and then extract the tooth according to right manner so as not to break it, nor give greater pain to the patient.
And if it is not forced out, then take one of those instruments, and place it under the area with ease and force the removal of it as is done at the beginning.
But if the tooth is broken or corroded, then you must wrap that part with cloth and tie it tightly at the end of a fine thread so that it does not get broken during your manipulation of it and hold it firmly.
And ensure that you operate precisely during the scarification of the circuit of all parts of the gum and keep your strength so as not to break any part of it, and return over the patient for the malice that is more than the first pain of it.
And beware that you do not do what some ignorant barbers do in their operations and boldness regarding the eradication of boils; for they do not administer what we have advised; which vain thoughts bring great illnesses upon men, which are harder to treat than boils, and the reasons behind their failures all, or some of those, or that they extract from certain bones of the jaw as we have testified with many examples.
And for the eradication of the boil, wash the mouth with vinegar or water mixed with salt.
And if there are fluxes of pus for this, as often happens, then take some ginger and sprinkle it over the wound. If this does not work, cauterize it.
The shape of the forceps and fine tongs used to extract a tooth at the beginning should be long, short, and thick, so as not to bend when you need to use them.
And they should be as when you close large openings so that when stretched they remain brief and tightly bound.
And they should be made of iron from India, straight and tightly bound, and in the ends of those, there are teeth which enter each other and stretch by descending force strongly, and some times the ends of those are in the shape of a duckbill which is called a ciconia, so they are strong in construction.

Chapter XXXII.
Of the treatment of prominent teeth above others.
When the teeth are prominent not according to their natural course, especially when they protrude in women, and particularly in elderly women; therefore consider: if a tooth is nearly touching another tooth and cannot be separated or aligned with it, then extract that tooth; but if it is not attached to another tooth, then use this instrument, the shape of which is shown here; and it resembles a pig's snout, made of Indian steel with an extremely sharp edge.
And make your incision with the instrument you will use to extract that tooth over several days due to its hardness, and ensure it is not too close to any other teeth.
And if the tooth is prominent and worn down, then file that part with an Indian steel file of which the shape is shown here:
And let it be all of iron and the margin sharpened; and made of small pointed pins like those of a file, on which the tooth is filed little by little over several days for ease, so that there is not another sharp tooth. And then line the one at the end, and sharpen the other with a few razors.
And if the tooth is such that a part of it is broken and hurts the tongue, then you must file that part so that the sharpness of that fracture is stopped and equalized, and be filled to prevent the tongue from being cut and the word from being corrupted.
Capitol.xxxiii.
For the restoration of decayed teeth with gold or silver foil.
When the front teeth are injured by concussion or removal through impact or extraction, and the patient cannot strengthen the area that is missing, and you have treated this with styptic medicines but your treatment has not been effective, then for those that are strong use gold foil and not silver, because silver becomes loose and may come out in a few days, while gold does not change over any amount of time.
And let the honey be in such subtlety and thickness according to the quantity that can enter between the teeth; and the form of the recao is that you take the honey and put twice its amount between two healthy teeth, and soon there will appear two tortuosity of the honey between two molar teeth, or one or spots, before the mesh reaches the healthy tooth from the other side. And then pass the thread into the part from which you started, and strengthen your hand with ease and skill before it is mangled.
And let your tension be such that when you pull the thread, it tightens the honey at the roots of the teeth so that none escapes.
And then divide the excess threads of the honey with forceps or tweezers, and add them to any place with care, and mix those and the hidden ones between the healthy tooth and the mangled one, so as not to injure the tongue. And then let it stay thus tied like a Roman.
If it is slipped or broken, strengthen that or those parts in such manner throughout its entire duration.
This is the form of the teeth and the figure of the extraction of two healthy teeth and two wisdom teeth, as you see these ligaments:

And it is not done by any mere artisan or fool.

Capitol.xxxiv.
On the incision of the ligament which is in the tongue and prohibiting speech.
This ligament which causes the tongue to be affected for some days is either natural, one that one is born with, or accidental and occurs due to a wound which has already healed.
And the operation is to open the mouth of the patient, their existing head in your hand; elevate their tongue, and then incise that nerve according to the width between which the tongue can be separated from its root.
And if there is any hardness or nodularity, and this is due to the consolidation of a boil, then you grip one end and incise it according to the width at which you have incised the nerve and where the nodularity has dissolved.
And make sure that no crack is made in the subcutaneous layer and that you incise here to allow the flow of pus.
And then wash the incision tracts with warm water or with vinegar or with wine; and then place the tongue to drain. If it is necessary, let the patient keep the tongue out overnight so that it does not become swollen again.
And if there is a flow of pus, place a glass triplex over the area to drain it; and if the pus continues to flow, then cauterize the area with a pointed cautery that suits this. And then the other causes are treated once it is healed.
Capitol.xxxv.
For the extraction of a ranula, I leave the tongue.
In some cases, when an abscess in the tongue occurs, I leave it untreated, prohibiting the tongue from its natural operation; and greatly it is enlarged until it fills the mouth.
And the operation for this is to open the mouth of the patient sixty degrees facing the sun and examine the abscess.
And if you see it of a dusky color or black, hard, to which the patient does not feel any sensation, then do not touch that area.
And if it is turning white, in which there is moisture, then you apply the probe to it, and incise that with a sharp knife, and incise all of it. And if the wound begins to bleed during your operation, then you stop above tigli trissat, which is vitriol, until the bleeding is reduced.
And then return to your work after you have brought him to completion, after he has been washed with vinegar and salt; and care for that with the other cure when it is healed.
Capitol. xxxvi.
For the extraction of abscesses in both ears and those that arise from the gola (throat) and other abscesses.
When pain arises in the gola (throat), they are glands which are clustered like ears, which occur externally and are named as two ears. When you treat them as we have said in the division and they do not heal, then consider if the abscess is hard, of dusky color, and has little sensation; then do not touch it with a iron.
And if it is of red color and the root is large, then do not touch that with iron due to the flow of blood; first let it mature, and then either you will incise it, or it will break by itself.
And if it is of white color, tender, and the root is fine, then it is to be incised.
And in the operation, you must consider before your operation whether the abscess has already rested and is completely cured or if it has decreased somewhat; then operate on the patient before the sun, with his head on your lap, and lifting his mouth, and a servant holding his tongue between their fingers, taking the noblest instrument of which this is the form:
And let it be made of silver or steel, and let it be sharp like a knife.
So when you press at that tongue and the abscess is shown to you, and cut over it quickly, then take a probe and place it in the abscess, and pull it outwards as far as you can. Another thing you pull from the tunics, and then incise that with the instrument of which this is the form:
Another thing you pull from the tunics, and then incise that with the instrument of which this is the form: and it is similar to forceps, but the ends are curved, so that the opening of each of those is in the straight part of the other, sharp points, which should be made of iron and well tempered.
If this instrument is not at your disposal, then incise that space from which this form comes: it should be sharp on one side, not on the other.
And since you have incised one wound, incise the other according to this manner of incision, and near the incision the sore should heal with water.
If there is a flow of blood, heal with water from the decoction of crushed colocynth or of hollyhock leaves and similar to those causes that constrict the flow of blood, and cure that once it is healed.
And sometimes sores appear in the groin or other abscesses elsewhere on the two ears, and incise those according to what is said and done in the incision of two wounds equally.
And I had already treated a woman with an abscess which was located in her groin, which abscess tended to have a brown color, with little sensation, and which had already closed her groin. The woman breathed freely, and had been prohibited from eating and drinking water, and she was close to death if more water were to remain for one or two days.
And the abscess had already been pressing so long that there were two handbreadths between where it would exit through two cuts.
Therefore I would incise the fistula completely and fix it in one of its ends, then pull that end, stretching the large portion. Next, I would incise the other part, and firmly hold the mouth of the other cut, grasping its tongue, and finally fix the end in the abscess.
And then I would cut a large part of it, but blood was flowing from it only in small amounts. Therefore the swelling was gone from that woman, and she began to drink water soon, and also eat food. Then I did not cease incising that abscess for a long time, and an abscess would recur in its place, which continued to form as long as the previous one lasted.
Therefore I enlarged and cauterized the swelling, then applied the plaster; next, I walked around and did not know what God had done to that nearby me.
Chapter XXXV.
Of the incision of the heel when it is swollen.
When a catarr (catarrah) affects the uvula, and it is swollen and long, then it is named perpendicular; if it is in the part large and round, then it is called a bubble.
When it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and you do not find your cure agreeable, and thus you often observe that the abscess caut has already passed away and become subtle, then probe that you incise that which is aggregated round; if it is at that length, and it bleeds, of dusky color or black, and is not a centimeter, then you should fear the incision of it, for there is fear concerning the illness.
And when you observe that according to the manner I have said of its whiteness and length, you should lance the illness and press the tongue of it with an instrument of which you determine its form and then fix the needle in the new site, and draw that down and incise that with one of the two instruments which are called in the incision of two abscesses.
And ensure that you do not insert it further than what is adjusted over the natural term of addition, for if you insert it more, you will alter its speech.
And near the insertion, use what we have described in the insertion of two fingers, and ensure that it is cured within.
And if the patient was frightened by the insertion, ensure that you use anesthetic in the cautery to alleviate his fear, and the way of applying the cautery is simply with sharp water. You should place the head of the patient in your lap, and then press the patient's tongue against the instrument as described. Additionally, take the sharp water from the section on cautery application, and apply it to the area without being too thin or subtle. Fill the cavity of the instrument according to its shape:
Let the external part of the cavity in which the medicine is applied be as wide as the handle of a ray, and place the instrument with the medicine over the vagina, while the patient opens his legs to allow saliva or mucus from his mouth to enter through the internal medicine, so that it does not decrease for any reason on the ligaments and affect him.
And then place your hand on the medicine, and express it over the uvula for half an hour between each time you let it darken due to the bite of the medicine.
And if you want, take some cloth and wrap it around the tip of the reed, then immerse the cloth in the medicine, and insert the reed with the cloth into a tube from above so that the cloth adheres to the tube. Do this as many times as needed to achieve the cauterization of the uvula you desire, and then let it dry and fall off in about three or four days.
And if you need to apply the medicine again, apply it, and then cauterize the area around the uvula with a wrapped cloth. Modify what is in the circuit of the uvula by the medicine, and wash it with water, and treat externally by soaking and internally with remedies until it heals.
And this method of treatment is safe and long-lasting without fear.
Some cases of tonsillitis are cured by what is finer than a cautery or incision, which is treated with subfumigation in this manner: take calamus, hyssop, origanum, rue, scikadis arabicus, camomile, powder and resemble those of the herbs, and adjust all those causes, or some of them, in one ointment, and be submerged in vinegar and boil; let the ointment be well beaten with decent honey, and let it be in the middle of the ointment a wick, over which is placed an instrument hollow of iron according to this manner; let it be made of silver or iron.
And let the extremity be inserted in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the tonsil above the uvula, so that the uvula becomes somewhat obscured.
And then it repeatedly passes over those spots several times while they are dry, and guard that you do not perform this cure at the beginning of the appearance of abscesses, for it would too tightly bind the abscess. You should not do this, but declare the abscess with a cautery.
But if you do not have this instrument at hand, then take a cane and place on its end a clog of wood, so that the opening of the patient's anus is blocked, for the wooden clog prevents the vapor from burning the opening.
And this cure is good for health.
Chapter XXXVIII.
On the extraction of thorns and what adheres in the wound and other causes.
Spots or thorns that adhere in the wound or from a thorny plant or some other cause.
Then carefully extract what is obvious and visible from the wound or thorn, by pressing the tongue with an instrument in front of the sun, so that you may know what is in the wound.
And what is not apparent and hidden in the wound, make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach, because if the cause attached to the wound is strong, it will be expelled through vomiting; or have the patient swallow a piece of napkin or flax cloth or a piece of dry bread; or take a piece of sponge dried with wine and tie it tightly with thread, and make the patient swallow that, for it will reach the place where the thorns are located and will be expelled. And take an eel and wrap it in honey, then place it inside and gently extract it; or take a pepper and gently insert it and then remove it.
And if none of these methods work as we have said, then use a lead instrument in this form:
And let it be as thick as a small finger, and at the end of it, have a cavity that you insert into his throat with ease.
And let his head be raised up, and guard that the touch of his bone in the throat reaches him, so that it affects him and either what covers the bone or the spine, or what that doctor places with his hand.
And instead, let the patient himself insert honey, by his knowledge of the place of the cause and cover it below, and pull his hand towards the instrument, all this according to the quantity which is prepared for him before it becomes ineffective.
Chapter XXXIX.
From the extraction of gouty fluid associated with the gout.
When the gouty fluid is treated with what we have said in the division of the treatment with medicines and you do not agree, consider at the heat of the gout during the gout attack in the sun, for you may have misunderstood the language of the instrument we have recommended.
Therefore, if you see the gouty fluid, extract it either through a small needle or with fine threads properly.
And if it is not possible to extract it through that, then take a concave cannula and insert it into the gout attack of the gout. Then place a burning iron in the concavity of the cannula, and do this as many times as necessary (until the gouty fluid is dead and stays out of the gout attack), and let the patient abstain from water for the entire day.
And then take a towel full of water, work its mouth into the area, and wash the area with it; and do not swallow any part of it, but let the water remain on the area for about an hour using your hand, as soon as the gouty fluid senses the water it will begin to drain.
If it is not already fomented with what we have recommended, then foment the thigh with cimeter or asafetida using the instrument we have recommended in the fomentation of uvula.
Do this, so that it may heal.
And another way of fomentation is that you take a bowl in which are burning coals and the bowl is covered with a cloth in the middle of which there is a hole, and place the end of the instrument in that hole; then proceed with the subfomentation; and place the thigh on the end of the cannula, and close its end so that the subfomentation does not get extinguished until you see that the subfomentation has reached the uvula, for the uvula will soon fall.
And if it does not heal, then you repeat the subfomentation several times, and abstain the thigh from drinking, eating salty foods and others, and do not drink water. It is necessary that this regimen be followed.
And this is the form of the instrument used to treat gout when it is seen; and it resembles tongs as you see them, but with some curvature in it: and the end of it is similar to the beak of a stork, which is wide, and on which it is filed with a file, so that when any cause is grasped, it does not slip.
Capitol.xl.
In which the essence of the speech concerning abscesses and their sections is found.
Abscesses are special kinds of boils, according to various methods as remembered, for each one in this treatise.
And they are varied in puncturing and sectioning them through two methods. Of these, one is according to the kind of abscesses themselves; and by this, they grasp the humors.
And the second method is according to the places where bodily accidents occur, for an abscess in the head is different from an abscess in the buttocks; and an abscess in a fleshly place is different from an abscess in a joint; and each one of them has its own judgment through operation.
And of abscesses, some which cover that they should not be punctured but rather wait for the maturation of the healing in those or their complement.
And of other abscesses which cover that they should be incised when crossed, and are not maturing according to their complement, thus like abscesses that are near joints, for an abscess when near a joint, the essence of it is prolonged into what is within that circuit, and greatly corrupts the ligaments or nerves of that joint, causing contraction of that limb; or it is near the main member, and if you delay the incision of it until its natural maturation for the main member; or it is near the anus, therefore incise that which is not matured; and it should not be incised raw, due to incomplete digestion, but one that is near the anus, so that no preon from it can extend into the inner parts of the anus, and a fistula may be formed, or what is done in its term until it is healed. And you should know the time for the incision of the abscess, and this is when it is matured.
And know that it is ripe when there is the reduction of pain and the cessation of fever, and the diminution of inflammation and pulse, and the acuteness of the head of the abscess, and other signs.
And know when to make the穿刺在脓肿下方的位置，并且是脓液从切口排出的时候。
And the puncture should be made along the length of the flesh or body, if the abscesses are in the parts near the groin or feet, and at the location of the groins, the cords of the nerves, the arches; and, otherwise, in all similar locations where there is no reflection; for in those that are reflective, use puncture according to that member.
And when the abscess is in a fleshly location, it is better to wait until the digestion of the pus is confirmed according to its natural course, as we have said; for if you puncture it before this, you will prolong the course of the pus and mucus, and increase the thickness and depth of the abscess.
More abscesses should be punctured according to the width of the flesh or body as necessity demands, or according to that from which the member suffers.
And see that you administer a small puncture in large abscesses, and a wide or multiple sections according to the diversity of the size of the abscesses.
And in other abscesses, see that the cord is returned to its cavity and tied, when this is done as with bread and done in such a way that it stays, just as one does for crops of melons and buboes.
And of those that are incised with a section having three angles; and of those in which an incision is made as the shape of a holly leaf, just as with abscesses of gout.
And of these, see those in which a round section and a crescent section are administered, and similar to those.
More for those in which none is done as such, where the abscesses are superficial, see that you puncture them with a superficial puncture, or flat one only.
And when the abscess is large and has already collected some healthy pus, you should pierce it and do not hesitate to extract all the foul matter at that time; having extracted one part, then pack the abscess on another day, and extract a larger part, and repeatedly do this until it is thoroughly drained.
And especially if the patient is of verdure virtue, or a woman in labor, or a small child, or an old person in decline, for the animal spirit has resolved into the exit of the healthy fluid, and greatly alleviates the illness, so you should openly proceed.
Take great care with this chapter, and when you make your puncture in which you perforate these abscesses, ensure that you clean the wounds and consider whether the wound of the abscess is small, or a flat section, then administer either herbs or cumin seeds; if the abscess is large, and the cracks of the puncture are deep, then you should pause to allow them to heal together.
And if in the abscess a part of the cord has been cut or you have concaved it in the circuit, then you should close it with old wool or with a thread made of linen, just as when you have drawn out bandages or roots, their humidity; strengthen it on the third day; and proceed with it and cure the area as what is appropriate from ointments until it is healed.
If you happen to have a flow of blood during the time of your operation, then you administer hot water mixed with wine in which you soak a cloth, and place that over the location of the blood flow for many minutes.
If the flow of blood persists, then you must administer treatment and care, as well as powders which I have recommended in many places of this our libel and division.
If it is in the time of winter, and the location of the abscess is near major nerves, then you should apply powders mixed with wine and oil using a cautery, and place those over the locations.
And if it is in the summer, and the locations are fatty, then you should place powders soaked in water and oil or in wine and oil, all of which should be applied within the first three days, as we have said, and then you should incise the abscess, cleanse it, and administer to it what is appropriate for its healing within the time that it heals.
And this is what is necessary regarding the knowledge of the treatment of abscesses universally, but according to the division I have already spoken of, all abscesses are treated in a particular manner by chapters singly.
Chapter XL.
Of the section on abscesses that occur in the vein of the head.
In the vein of the head, small abscesses occur, and they contain nodules which are formed; and the nature of these nodules is spotted.
And they are lumps, and among them are those that contain a humidity resembling lime. And among them are those that contain a humidity resembling dust, similar to it; and among them are those that are hardened, hard.
And in the section of all, and in the extraction of these, there is no fear, just as you should not fear the extraction of these without causing any resistance.
And the operation for the section of these is that you puncture them with an instrument in the form which is close at hand, which is called a lancet until you know it contains fluid.
If what is contained is humidity, then section that with an instrument along its length for a superficial section in this manner:
And begin in the section of line B between line G. Then as the humidity is evacuated, you scratch that skin which contains that humidity, and leave none of that cause of all, because too many times returns if left of that any cause.
And then immerse it in Egyptian ointment if present, and otherwise in water and salt; then apply it to the wound and leave it there for another day, because with it you will dissolve all that is rotten of that skin.
And then repeatedly apply it to that part with Egyptian ointment gently if you need it, confident that there is no rotten cause of that skin; after that, cure the wound with ointment while it is healing.

Capitol. XLIX.

Capitalize the abscess which has occurred due to nerve injury.

Capitol. lii.
On the cure of swelling around the navel.
Swelling around the navel is caused by various reasons; it may be due to fissures in the cartilage which is above the abdomen, and protrudes the membrane or intestine depending on where the other ruptures are; or it may be due to a wound that flows from a vein or artery as previously mentioned, or due to constricted fatty tissue.
If it is due to a cartilage fissure and a swelling of the membrane, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body; and the pain is severe, often appearing in various locations. And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then place that part as we have described in greater diversity of position, and when you press that part against the thighs, it is concealed, and then return; firmly hold it there so, and make a strong movement for washing and vigorous work.
And if due to humidity, then it is loose and not concealed when you press it with your hand, nor is it compressed or believed.
And if due to scab, then in this case the abscess appears blackish in color declining.
And if due to no flesh, then the abscess is severe, large, and hard, and is inserted according to a quantity.
And if due to humidity, then the touch of it is loose.
And the operation on it is that you consider whether the prominence of the navel is due to an arrow wound, or a vein, or due to humidity; then know that you must be careful about treating it, for there is fear and dread as you were taught in the Capitol where I said about abscesses from arrows and veins.
And if the prominence of the navel is due to the intestine or the fabric, then command the patient to hold their breath, and stand extended; and then touch around the entire circumference of the navel, and command the one standing between your hands to hold them in place, and surround with a wide strip over the area you marked with the touch; and extend the size of the abscess upwards by about an inch; and place something strong or soft on the way to bind decently.
And then extend the widest part of the abscess over the membrane and insert your finger into that indentation to feel for the intestine; if you have already touched it and protected it with the membrane, then carefully extract it and push the intestine into the internal parts of the abdomen.
And if you have touched the fabric, then take it with an inch; and incise the superfluous parts of it.
But if it is contrary to your artery or vein, then surround that spot, and then return to your operation; take two needles and place them in those strong threads, and insert two needles into the circumference you made around the abscess in a cross shape, making sure they penetrate; and then strengthen the abscess in four parts over the needles.
And if you wish, hold the needles and let the place where the extended flesh may fall in by itself; or incise that which is thin-skinned and let it flow out, and then cover it with ointments until it heals.
And if the prominence of the navel is due to flesh nowhere in it or by humidity, then you should treat the abscess as we have said and drain the pus or moisture which you find in it, and then cover it with what heals and strengthens the area.

Capitol. liv.

And the first ones said that it should be done as we have recommended for the hernia that is inside; which is that you tie the vessels near the section over there where there is facilitation; and then dry in the middle place by applying a poultice with what I operate there, so that the vessels fall.

Chapter LXVII.
Of the disorder that occurs in the ankles.
In some cases, there is a rupture in the ankles as we have said, and cover the area with a cloth.
And the genii do not attribute any cause of the hernias to the genii; and if they do, it is very little; and return them to their place at all times.
But if the time is prolonged, there is an adjusted fissure in the capsule through which to return the hernia into the capsule; and this happens due to the extension of the capsule, which occurs in the ankles as we have said. The cause is that the capsule becomes stretched, and further, it softens, causing suppuration, and covering the area.
And the treatment of it is with a cautery as in the preceding description of it.
And sometimes it is cured by applying iron according to this manner: and it is that the patient lies on his back between your knees, and then dry the area of the rupture of the abscesses emits by seepage according to the breadth as per the quantity of three digits.
And strengthen the white cloth that is under the cushion once it is uncovered.
And place the rod and hold it above the area where the cloth is emitting, and press it against the front of the abdomen.

Capitol. lxviii.
On the mollification of the scrotal skin.
When the scrotal skin becomes spotted or discolored in some men, it is mollified accordingly because the flesh between those areas is also mollified, and the condition of this is observed.
Then it is necessary for the one who is overseeing the treatment to have the patient lie in a position suitable for their condition, and completely expose the scrotum which is mollified over the natural scrotal skin; and then carefully suture the two edges together.
And if you wish, begin the closure of the excess scrotal skin with three or four stitches and a final suture.
Then carefully cut between the sutures; and continue to treat the other wounds until they heal and the stitches dissolve.
Capitol lxix.
Of castration.
Know that castration in our law is excommunicated, but by cause it is allowed to me to remember it in this treatise; and the remembrance of it is necessary for two reasons, one of which is that when asked about it as a doctor, one knows the cure for whom it happens. The other reason is that we may have necessity to castrate other animals for our young ones, such as bulls, goats, pigs, and similar to animals.
And therefore, it is said that castration can be performed in two ways: either by traction or by incision.
But in that which is performed by traction, the way of the operation is to tie the beast by its tail in water until the testicles are softened and relaxed. And then take those with your hand until they are relaxed and do not appear to have marks upon touch.
In castration performed due to fissure and secution, ensure that you have the beast and press the cord of the testicles with your left hand.
Then lift the suspensory ligament, and incise over each groove between two testicles.
Then incise those abscesses that have formed in each place. And do not incise any of those on the scrotum for any cause, but incise only the thin one which is over the veins.
And this method of castration is better which is performed by traction, for traction firmly leaves no cause of the testicles, because the beast desires copulation.
Then cure the wound while it is healing.
Capitol.lix.
On the cure of hermaphroditism.
Hermaphroditism in males occurs according to two methods: one where a fourth testicle appears between the two testicles, resembling that of a female with its appearance.
And sometimes urine flows from that area in the region of the testicles.
In women, it is special: and the swelling in the groin is such that it appears like two testicles of a man, slightly different in size, with some hardness at the outer part like the scrotum of a man with its two testicles.
And the cure is of three kinds: two for men and one for women. And you must incise those tight tissues where the tension of that area escapes, and then treat those with the cure for other wounds.
And in the second kind for men from which urine flows from the region of the testicles, neither cure nor operation is needed.

Then you should have the superfluous mucus of the phlegm in your hand or cupped with your hand and removed.
And do not finish with cupping, especially on the back, so that no flow of sweat occurs.

More hidden flesh is flesh that grows in the horror of the womb until it fills that space, and a larger cyst is situated outside according to the likeness of a coconut (and for this some first called it "hidden illness"); therefore, we should cut it as we cut phlegm, and care for it until it is healed.
Capitol.lix.
Of the care of alum disease.
Alratica is when the hymen of the woman is not perforated, or is only slightly torn. And it can be natural or accidental.
Accidental is due to a malady which has preceded, and that one is caused by flesh not fitting well or by a thin or thick membrane.
It is caused in the region of the kidney, or in its flanks, or in the upper part of it, or in the lower part of it, and you prohibit coitus and copulation and childbirth, and especially you prohibit menstruation.
The knowledge of that is made by looking at the midwife, if the obstruction is obvious, promptly; but if it is not obvious, then you search for that among the thighs or in the groin.
But if the obstruction is due to a thin membrane, and is close to the two lips, then you open and rupture that.
And you place powders over the two lips, and then place your hands on the indices of both sides near them.
And the woman is on her back, her thighs extended, and then spread the two lips with force while that thin membrane is broken and the obstruction is opened.
And then take wool and soak it in oil and place it over the area, and keep someone there to prevent the incised area from healing too quickly.
And if the abscess is large and thick, then you must incise it with a lancet or a leaf of myrtle.

And keep it for a few days and administer water that has been boiled.

And sometimes accidents occur in the natural growth of other tissues, then you must incise according to this method. But if this is due to a malignant apstema, the apstema which is in the greater must not be treated by any method that could aggravate it.

Chapter LXXVI.
On the extraction of the fetus when it is dead.

Place the fingers accordingly: then consider if the fetus is prepared to be delivered through its head, and then place the fingers in the folds of its neck, or on its collarbone, or in its mouth, or on its palate, or leave the beard area, or on the furcula, or at the appropriate locations of the ribs, or leave the hypochondria.

And I have already seen a woman in her belly where one child was dead, and near that fire another pregnancy began, and the fire is dead for the second. It happens that after a long time an abscess in the groin; and inflammation begins within that open fire, and starts to discharge pus.

For the treatment of fistulas that discharge.
The fistulas that discharge pus below are nodotic and gross, those that discharge near the buttocks or in the space of one side.
And it is a fistula or spots.
And when that nodosity is old and flows from watery white or subtle rot, sometimes these fistulas penetrate.
And those that penetrate are known by what is caused by them through the discharge and by wind condition; sometimes the patient complains of the discharge, and strongly suffer from those worms.
And of these fistulas, sometimes in the space they penetrate into the bladder, and into the flesh of the groin; and of those that penetrate into the joint of the thigh and into the notch of the buttock.
And to know whether a penetrating fistula goes into the buttock or not, you should insert your finger into the buttock and gently probe with a fine stick of reed or iron in the fistula when there is no pus.
But if there is hardness, then insert a thin rod of lead or horsehair between that tent and feel the rod or hair with your finger.
And if you do not feel that at all and there is no cause for obstruction or worm or hardness, as we have said, then know that it is non-penetrant, and then apply a remedy.
And when the fistula is penetrant into the bladder or into the flesh of the groin, then its significance is dysuria from that and prohibition thereof until the area with medicine is consolidated.
But if it is penetrant into the junction of the thigh or into the bone and causes pain in the circuit, then the sign thereof is that the probe passes into here if there is no hardness in the bone, and pain in the circuit of the limb; and that pus comes out continuously; and that it does not respond to that medicine, nor is it consolidated with ointment.
And in all those penetrant fistulas, complete cure is not always achieved, and the cure of these is hard work and the diligence of the surgeons over them which must be firm.
In those that are not penetrating and not ancient, heal them with iron as I will recount to you later, and what I have already said and advised.
And it is that the patient lies on his back and elevates his legs between them, the thighs inclined towards the abdomen of the patient, and near insert a lead tube or an iron one if it is in the tortuous fistula, so you can feel the place where the tube passes.
And if the patient feels pain around the throat, then you should insert the thumb as directed into the throat.
And if you feel in the thumb that the tube is already by itself fully exposed and penetrating, or if you feel something between the thumb and the siphac or flesh, then you can certainly determine that it is penetrating; and then do not work on that, for healing does not occur there, as we have said.
However, some say that it is healed in some men after the third day.
And for the treatment by which hope is given of healing, you should use a fine cautery according to the size of the fistula as described before, and insert that fire into the fistula until it reaches around the bowels; then repeatedly insert it two or three times until you know that all those tissues adjacent to the fistula are thoroughly cauterized and appear like feather reeds.
And then cure that which is with bands wrapped around the limb until all those tissues that are cauterized are healed, and then cure that which is with medicines, the flesh generating and consolidating, and if it is healed, well; and if not, then it will not be cured in some time by another treatment.
And if the tent enters but does not penetrate deeply, you have described it as being in the anus. Of the treatment of wounds.
And I have already said in the division of the treatment of wounds what pertains to the free treatment and medicines according to necessity.
Therefore, it is said that wounds are diverse according to what they are caused by and according to the place where the plaques occur.

More specifically, the wounds that occur in parts of the body are thus: a wound that occurs on the head, or the neck, or the foot, or the belly, or the thigh, or something similar to those of the limbs.
And I am therefore recounting the treatment of some wounds so that you apply that reasoning and rule to other wounds.

And the incision is made on the opposite side of the wounded area; and one must guard against swelling and edema from fluids and large foods.

Chapter on Fractures: When an injury occurs in the head.
The species of fractures are spots, and their figures are diverse, and the causes are distinct, for some fracture is made by spaza impact, and the impact obstructs all the bone within the socket, which leaves the bone thus as in the wood, and by this this species is named ascial; or spaza incides some part of the bone, and incides the flesh but does not pass the incision into the marrow thereof; and this species of fracture is named levatio absolute.
The plague of these two fractures is great or small, and of the fracture that is contricious or abrasive; its cause is impact from a fall or building on stone, and they resemble each other.
This fracture is penetrating and already approaches the periosteum which leaves the bone; or it is in the face of the bone, and the plague of these two fractures is great or small.
And of the fracture, it is weakened in the bone, in the subtlety of the small hair [cancellous bone], and by this it is named this species of fracture capillary.
And this is a fracture that is caused by compression or impact, resembling such that some layer of the bone enters the internal parts, and it occurs in the concave location as when you strike a metal plate and its entry into the internal parts.
And this is most commonly found in the bodies of humid bones, such as those of children.

For the restoration of the nose when it is broken.

Chapter IV.
On the restoration of the jaw when broken.

Chapter 12.
On the restoration of fractures of the arm.

And when the fracture of the leg is broken, I leave the fracture bad, and the healing of it is difficult.
